The Oryza bacterial artificial chromosome library resource: construction and analysis of 12 deep-coverage large-insert BAC libraries that represent the 10 genome types of the genus Oryza. Genome Res. 16, 140–147 (2006)." href="/articles/ng.736#ref-CR49" id="ref-link-section-d52119e3142">49</a></sup>). Ligation products were transformed into DH10B T1 phage-resistant <i>Escherichia coli</i> cells (Invitrogen) and plated on Lysogeny broth agar that contained chloramphenicol (12.5 μg ml<sup>−1</sup>), X-gal (20 mg ml<sup>−1</sup>) and Isopropyl β-D-1-thiogalactopyranoside (0.1 M). For characteristics, quality assessment and estimated genome coverage see the <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/ng.736#MOESM2">Supplementary Note</a> and <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/ng.736#MOESM2">Supplementary Table 1</a>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec14">Genome sequencing.</h3><p>The genome was sequenced using a genome-wide shotgun strategy. All data were generated using next-generation sequencers: Roche/454 GSFLX (×16.5 coverage) and Illumina GAIIx (×44 coverage), except for data from BAC ends (×0.2 coverage), which were produced by paired-end sequencing of cloned inserts using Sanger technology on ABI3730xl sequencers (<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/ng.736#MOESM2">Supplementary Note</a> and <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/ng.736#MOESM2">Supplementary Table 2</a>).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec15">Genome assembly and automatic error corrections with Solexa/Illumina reads.</h3><p>Sanger and 454 reads were assembled with Newbler version 2.3. From the initial 26,519,827 reads, 80.65% (21,387,691) were assembled by Newbler. The 454 assembly was improved by automatic error corrections with Solexa/Illumina reads, which have a different bias in error type, as described previously<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 50" title="Aury, J.M. et al. High quality draft sequences for prokaryotic genomes using a mix of new sequencing technologies. BMC Genomics 9, 603 (2008)." href="/articles/ng.736#ref-CR50" id="ref-link-section-d52119e3182">50</a></sup>. Short-read sequences were aligned on the cocoa genome assembly using the SOAP software (with a seed size of 12 bp and a maximum gap size allowed on a read of 3 bp). Only uniquely mapped reads were retained (<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/ng.736#MOESM2">Supplementary Note</a>).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec16">Estimation of nuclear DNA content by flow cytometry.</h3><p>The genome sizes of B97-61/B2 and a panel of diverse cocoa clones were estimated by flow cytometry<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 51" title="Marie, D. &amp; Brown, S.C. A cytometric exercise in plant DNA histograms, with 2C values for 70 species. Biology of the Cell/Under the Auspices of the European Cell Biology Organization 78, 41–51 (1993)." href="/articles/ng.736#ref-CR51" id="ref-link-section-d52119e3198">51</a></sup>. Leaves of studied samples and internal standards were chopped with a razor blade and then stained using propidium iodide. DNA content of 5,000–10,000 stained nuclei was determined using a CyFlow SL3 flow cytometer with a 532-nm green solid state laser (100 mWatt). The monoploid C-value (1C) was calculated and expressed in Mb using the conversion factor 1 pg DNA = 978 Mb (<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/ng.736#MOESM2">Supplementary Note</a>).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec17">Anchoring of the assembly in the genetic map.</h3><p>A consensus map was established from two progenies: an F1 progeny of 256 individuals (UPA 402 × UF676) and an F2 progeny of 136 individuals recently produced (Scavina 6 × ICS1). The F1 progeny was previously used to established the cocoa reference map, which includes 600 markers<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 52" title="Pugh, T. et al. A new cacao linkage map based on codominant markers: development and integration of 201 new microsatellite markers. Theor. Appl. Genet. 108, 1151–1161 (2004)." href="/articles/ng.736#ref-CR52" id="ref-link-section-d52119e3213">52</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 53" title="Fouet, O. et al. Structural characterization and mapping of functional EST-SSR markers in Theobroma cacao, in the press." href="/articles/ng.736#ref-CR53" id="ref-link-section-d52119e3216">53</a></sup>. New SSR and SNP markers were mapped in these two progenies, and a consensus map including 1,259 markers was established<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 54" title="Allegre, M. et al. A high-density consensus genetic map for Theobroma cacao L., in the press." href="/articles/ng.736#ref-CR54" id="ref-link-section-d52119e3220">54</a></sup>. BLAT software was used to align the markers of the genetic map with the scaffolds (<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/ng.736#MOESM2">Supplementary Note</a>).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec18">Prediction of transposable elements.</h3><p>The annotation of transposable elements in the cocoa genome was achieved in two stages. First, a combination of <i>de novo</i> analyses (for example, LTR_finder, LTRharvest, MUST (see <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="section anchor" href="/articles/ng.736#Sec10">URLs</a>)) and extrinsic comparisons (BLAST) was conducted. Then, a <i>de novo</i> approach was used to construct highly repeated elements from the 3,220,522 unassembled reads. A total of 67,575 transposable elements were annotated (<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/ng.736#MOESM2">Supplementary Note</a>).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec19"><i>In situ</i> hybridization of transposable element probes.</h3><p>FISH was performed on mitotic metaphase spreads prepared from meristem root tip cells. The probes were labeled with Alexa-488 dUTP and Alexa-594 dUTP by random priming (Fisher Bioblock Scientific) and the <i>in situ</i> hybridizations were performed according to D'Hont <i>et al</i>.<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 55" title="D'hont, A. et al. Characterisation of the double genome structure of modern sugarcane cultivars (Saccharum spp.) by molecular cytogenetics. Mol. Gen. Genet. 250, 405–413 (1996)." href="/articles/ng.736#ref-CR55" id="ref-link-section-d52119e3264">55</a></sup> (<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/ng.736#MOESM2">Supplementary Note</a>).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec20">Prediction of protein-coding genes.</h3><p>Gene structures were predicted using EUGene<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 12" title="Foissac, S. et al. Genome annotation in plants and fungi: EuGène as a model platform. Curr. Bioinform. 3, 87–97 (2008)." href="/articles/ng.736#ref-CR12" id="ref-link-section-d52119e3279">12</a></sup>. Translation start sites and RNA splice sites were predicted by SpliceMachine<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 56" title="Degroeve, S., Saeys, Y., De Baets, B., Rouzé, P. &amp; Van de Peer, Y. SpliceMachine: predicting splice sites from high-dimensional local context representations. Bioinformatics 21, 1332–1338 (2005)." href="/articles/ng.736#ref-CR56" id="ref-link-section-d52119e3283">56</a></sup>. Available <i>T. cacao</i> ESTs were aligned onto the scaffolds using GenomeThreader<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 57" title="Gremme, G., Brendel, V., Sparks, M.E. &amp; Kurtz, S. Engineering a software tool for gene structure prediction in higher organisms. Inf. Softw. Technol. 47, 965–978 (2005)." href="/articles/ng.736#ref-CR57" id="ref-link-section-d52119e3290">57</a></sup>. Similarities to proteins from Swiss-Prot, TAIR, Malvacae GenBank extraction, <i>Glycine max</i> high confidence gene models<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 58" title="Schmutz, J. et al. Genome sequence of the palaeopolyploid soybean. Nature 463, 178–183 (2010)." href="/articles/ng.736#ref-CR58" id="ref-link-section-d52119e3298">58</a></sup> and translated <i>T. cacao</i> EST contigs were searched using BLASTX. Similarities to <i>A. thaliana</i>, <i>Gossypium</i>, <i>V. vinifera</i>, <i>Citrus</i> and <i>T. cacao</i> ESTs were searched using TBLASTX. A total of 50,582 genes were predicted, giving a final count of 28,798 <i>T. cacao</i> genes after filtering (<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/ng.736#MOESM2">Supplementary Note</a>).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec21">Gene family analysis.</h3><p>Protein domains were searched using InterProscan against the InterPro database. Cocoa, <i>Arabidopsis</i>, grape, poplar and soybean Best Blast Mutual Hit (BBMH) were computed, and protein clustering was done using OrthoMCL<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 59" title="Li, L., Stoeckert, C.J. &amp; Roos, D.S. OrthoMCL: identification of ortholog groups for eukaryotic genomes. Genome Res. 13, 2178–2189 (2003)." href="/articles/ng.736#ref-CR59" id="ref-link-section-d52119e3338">59</a></sup>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec22">Synteny and duplication analysis.</h3><p>Arabidopsis, grape, poplar, soybean and papaya proteomes were aligned using an approach based on BLASTP in order to identify accurate paralogous and orthologous relationships<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 44" title="Salse, J., Abrouk, M., Murat, F., Quraishi, U.M. &amp; Feuillet, C. Improved criteria and comparative genomics tool provide new insights into grass paleogenomics. Briefings Bioinf. 10, 619–630 (2009)." href="/articles/ng.736#ref-CR44" id="ref-link-section-d52119e3351">44</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 45" title="Salse, J. et al. Reconstruction of monocotelydoneous proto-chromosomes reveals faster evolution in plants than in animals. Proc. Natl. Acad. Sci. USA 106, 14908–14913 (2009)." href="/articles/ng.736#ref-CR45" id="ref-link-section-d52119e3354">45</a></sup>. K<sub>S</sub> divergence (million year ago (MYA) scale) for paralogous and orthologous gene pairs as well as speciation events dating were calculated with PAML<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 60" title="Goldman, N. &amp; Yang, Z. A codon-based model of nucleotide substitution for protein-coding DNA sequences. Mol. Biol. Evol. 11, 725–736 (1994)." href="/articles/ng.736#ref-CR60" id="ref-link-section-d52119e3360">60</a></sup>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec23">Accession codes.</h3><p>The <i>Theobroma cacao</i> whole-genome sequences are deposited in the EMBL, GenBank and DDBJ databases under accession numbers <a href="http://getentry.ddbj.nig.ac.jp/getentry?database=ddbj&amp;accession_number=CACC01000001%96CACC01025912">CACC01000001–CACC01025912</a>. A genome browser and further information on the project are available from <a href="http://cocoagendb.cirad.fr/gbrowse">http://cocoagendb.cirad.fr/gbrowse</a> and <a href="http://cocoagendb.cirad.fr">http://cocoagendb.cirad.fr</a>.</p></div></div></section>

Bocca, D.C., R.R., M.T., J.M.A., K.G., I.K., J.-M.A. and C.L. performed material preparation and multiplication, DNA and RNA extractions, genotyping, genetic mapping and anchoring of the assembly.</p><p>D.K., J.S.S.A., W.G. and X.S. performed BAC libraries.</p><p>J.-M.A., J.P., S.C.S., J.E.C., M.K., L.G. and W.R.M. performed sequencing and assembly.</p><p>X.A., G.D., J.G., M. Brown performed repeated elements and miRNA analyses.</p><p>M.R.-G., M. Bourge, S. Brown and A. D'Hont performed in situ hybridizations and genome-size evaluations.</p><p>M.J.G., G.D., T.L., S.N.M., M.R., A. Dievart, Z.S., X.S. and Y.Z. performed gene family analyses.</p><p>J.S., M.
